        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(crypt_activate_by_signed_key) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_crypt_activate_by_signed_key found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_crypt_activate_by_signed_key)
                #error "__builtin_crypt_activate_by_signed_key not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(crypt_activate_by_signed_key)
            __builtin_crypt_activate_by_signed_key;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(close_range) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_close_range found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_close_range)
                #error "__builtin_close_range not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(close_range)
            __builtin_close_range;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(__secure_getenv) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin___secure_getenv found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin___secure_getenv)
                #error "__builtin___secure_getenv not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(__secure_getenv)
            __builtin___secure_getenv;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(fsconfig) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_fsconfig found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_fsconfig)
                #error "__builtin_fsconfig not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(fsconfig)
            __builtin_fsconfig;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(getttynam) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_getttynam found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_getttynam)
                #error "__builtin_getttynam not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(getttynam)
            __builtin_getttynam;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(getsgnam) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_getsgnam found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_getsgnam)
                #error "__builtin_getsgnam not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(getsgnam)
            __builtin_getsgnam;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(llseek) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_llseek found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_llseek)
                #error "__builtin_llseek not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(llseek)
            __builtin_llseek;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(ntp_gettime) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_ntp_gettime found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_ntp_gettime)
                #error "__builtin_ntp_gettime not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(ntp_gettime)
            __builtin_ntp_gettime;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(pidfd_send_signal) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_pidfd_send_signal found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_pidfd_send_signal)
                #error "__builtin_pidfd_send_signal not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(pidfd_send_signal)
            __builtin_pidfd_send_signal;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(setprogname) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_setprogname found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_setprogname)
                #error "__builtin_setprogname not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(setprogname)
            __builtin_setprogname;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(sched_setattr) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_sched_setattr found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_sched_setattr)
                #error "__builtin_sched_setattr not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(sched_setattr)
            __builtin_sched_setattr;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(statx) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_statx found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_statx)
                #error "__builtin_statx not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(statx)
            __builtin_statx;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }

Code:
 
        int main(void) {

        /* With some toolchains (MSYS2/mingw for example) the compiler
         * provides various builtins which are not really implemented and
         * fall back to the stdlib where they aren't provided and fail at
         * build/link time. In case the user provides a header, including
         * the header didn't lead to the function being defined, and the
         * function we are checking isn't a builtin itself we assume the
         * builtin is not functional and we just error out. */
        #if !1 && !defined(ioperm) && !0
            #error "No definition for __builtin_ioperm found in the prefix"
        #endif

        #ifdef __has_builtin
            #if !__has_builtin(__builtin_ioperm)
                #error "__builtin_ioperm not found"
            #endif
        #elif ! defined(ioperm)
            __builtin_ioperm;
        #endif
        return 0;
        }
